## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration given state (x, v) and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (nonlinear) second-order oscillator: x' = v, v' = f(x,v,t). Common structures include restoring-force terms in x, damping terms in v, and optional external/parametric driving via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator (SHO): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hookean restoring force, conservative)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Constant bias / equilibrium shift: dv_dt = -c0 * (x - c1) - c2 * v (oscillation about shifted equilibrium)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (stronger amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping (quadratic drag-like): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-squared dissipation)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (odd-in-v damping at larger speeds)
- Coulomb (dry) friction model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (smoothed sign(v) friction; stick-slip tendency)
- Simple pendulum (bounded restoring force): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance / chaos regimes)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (Mathieu-type behavior, parametric resonance)
- van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Liénard-type oscillator family: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation + nonlinear restoring)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: conservative oscillator restoring terms are typically odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3); even-in-x terms often imply asymmetry or shifted equilibrium.
- Damping symmetry: dissipative forces are typically odd in v (e.g., -c*v, -c*v**3, -c*v*Abs(v)); even-in-v terms usually indicate modeling artifacts.
- Conservative vs nonconservative cue: if dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is conservative with energy exchange between x and v; v-terms imply dissipation or self-excitation.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle signature: factors like (c0 - x**2)*v indicate negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude (van der Pol–like).
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: inclusion of x**3 (Duffing) produces frequency shifts with amplitude; fitting often benefits from odd polynomial restoring terms.
- Bounded restoring force indicator: sin(c*x) suggests geometric constraints (pendulum-like) and prevents unbounded restoring growth at large |x|.
- External drive identification: explicit periodic functions of t (sin/cos) add energy; look for resonance when drive frequency matches natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation fingerprint: a coefficient multiplying x that varies with t (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) can create instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Dry friction behavior: near-constant-magnitude opposing force appears as sign(v); smooth approximations use v/(Abs(v)+c) to avoid discontinuities in regression.

- an \(x^3\) term (coefficient \(-3.9976552615\))
- a \(v^3\) term (coefficient \(-0.0883678101\))
- a \(v\sin(x)\) term (coefficient \(-0.1959337251\)) with argument exactly \(x\) (phase shifts not allowed unless they still equal \(\sin x\) for all \(x\))
- a \(\sin(v)\) term (coefficient \(-0.1959337251\)) — crucially, this is **\(\sin(v)\)**, not \(v\sin(\cdot)\), not \(\sin(\cdot x)\), etc.

Also, variables can be negative, so anything involving `Abs(v)` generally cannot be turned into \(\sin(v)\) or a plain polynomial globally.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO30)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - beta*sin(v) - omega0**c1*x**c2
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.0884*v³ - 0.1959*v*sin(x) - 3.998*x³ - 0.1959*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³` (coefficient ≈ -0.0884)
2. `v*sin(x)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1959)
3. `x³` (coefficient ≈ -3.998)
4. `sin(v)` (coefficient ≈ -0.1959)

The key challenge is that `sin(v)` is a standalone term (not multiplied by another variable). Let me check each candidate.

**Key observation about sin(v):** The GT contains `-β*sin(v)`. This is a function of `v` alone. For small `v`, `sin(v) ≈ v - v³/6 + v⁵/120 - ...`. But we need EXACT equivalence, not approximations.

Let me analyze candidates systematically:

**Candidates 1-9:** These contain `v*sin(c*x + c)` which gives `v*sin(x)` (good), and various terms for the `sin(v)` part.

- **Candidates 1-4:** Have `v⁵*exp(c*|v|)`. This cannot equal `sin(v)` for all `v`. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidates 5-6:** Have `v/(c+|v|)` terms. These are odd functions of `v`, but `v/(c+|v|)` cannot reproduce `sin(v)` exactly. **NO MATCH**
- **Candidates 7-9:** Have `v⁵*cos(c*t)`. Setting `c8=0` makes `cos(c8*t)=1`, giving `c7*v⁵`. But `v⁵` ≠ `sin(v)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 10-19:** These use `v*exp(c*x)*cos(c*x)` or polynomial terms in `v*x^n`. None of these can produce both `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)` exactly. The term `v*exp(c6*x)*cos(c7*x)` cannot equal `v*sin(x)` for all `x` (exponential times cosine ≠ sine). **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidates 20-25:** Use `v*cos(c*t)*|v|^n` and `v*x³` terms. Cannot produce `sin(v)` or `v*sin(x)`. **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 26-50:** Various combinations of `v/(c+|v|)`, `x³*exp(c*v)`, `v*|v|`, `v*x^n`, `v*sin(c*x+c)`, etc.

For any candidate to match GT, it must produce:
1. `v*sin(x)` — needs a `v*sin(cx+c)` term
2. `sin(v)` — needs a `sin(v)` term or something exactly equivalent

None of the candidates contain a standalone `sin(v)` term. The candidates try to approximate `sin(v)` using:
- `v⁵*exp(c*|v|)` — not equal to `sin(v)`
- `v/(c+|v|)` — not equal to `sin(v)`
- `v*|v|` — not equal to `sin(v)`
- `v⁵` — not equal to `sin(v)`
- Polynomial terms in `v` — cannot equal `sin(v)`
- `v*exp(cx)*cos(cx)` — function of both `v` and `x`, not `sin(v)`

Since `sin(v)` is transcendental and none of these basis functions can exactly reproduce it, **no candidate matches**.
